    11	#define CHAISCRIPT_THREADING_HPP_
    12	
    13	#include <unordered_map>
    14	
    15	#ifndef CHAISCRIPT_NO_THREADS
    16	#include <mutex>
    17	#include <shared_mutex>
    18	#include <thread>
    19	#else
    20	#ifndef CHAISCRIPT_NO_THREADS_WARNING
    21	#pragma message("ChaiScript is compiling without thread safety.")
    22	#endif
    23	#endif
    24	
    25	#include "chaiscript_defines.hpp"
    26	
    27	/// \file
    28	///
    29	/// This file contains code necessary for thread support in ChaiScript.
    30	/// If the compiler definition CHAISCRIPT_NO_THREADS is defined then thread safety
    31	/// is disabled in ChaiScript. This has the result that some code is faster, because mutex locks are not required.
    32	/// It also has the side effect that the chaiscript::ChaiScript object may not be accessed from more than
    33	/// one thread simultaneously.
    34	
    35	/// If threading is enabled, then this namespace contains std thread classes.
    36	/// If threading is not enabled, then stubbed in wrappers that do nothing are provided.
    37	/// This allows us to avoid \#ifdef code in the sections that need thread safety.
    38	namespace chaiscript::detail::threading {
    39	#ifndef CHAISCRIPT_NO_THREADS
    40	
    41	  template<typename T>
    42	  using unique_lock = std::unique_lock<T>;
    43	
    44	  template<typename T>
    45	  using shared_lock = std::shared_lock<T>;
    46	
    47	  template<typename T>
    48	  using lock_guard = std::lock_guard<T>;
    49	
    50	  using std::shared_mutex;
    51	
    52	  using std::mutex;
    53	
    54	  using std::recursive_mutex;
    55	
    56	  /// Typesafe thread specific storage. If threading is enabled, this class uses a mutex protected map. If
    57	  /// threading is not enabled, the class always returns the same data, regardless of which thread it is called from.
    58	  template<typename T>
    59	  class Thread_Storage {
    60	  public:
    61	    Thread_Storage() = default;
    62	    Thread_Storage(const Thread_Storage &) = delete;
    63	    Thread_Storage(Thread_Storage &&) = delete;
    64	    Thread_Storage &operator=(const Thread_Storage &) = delete;
    65	    Thread_Storage &operator=(Thread_Storage &&) = delete;
    66	
    67	    ~Thread_Storage() { t().erase(this); }
    68	
    69	    inline const T *operator->() const noexcept { return &(t()[this]); }
    70	
    71	    inline const T &operator*() const noexcept { return t()[this]; }
    72	
    73	    inline T *operator->() noexcept { return &(t()[this]); }
    74	
    75	    inline T &operator*() noexcept { return t()[this]; }
    76	
    77	    void *m_key;
    78	
    79	  private:
    80	    /// todo: is it valid to make this noexcept? The allocation could fail, but if it
    81	    /// does there is no possible way to recover
    82	    static std::unordered_map<const void *, T> &t() noexcept {
    83	      static thread_local std::unordered_map<const void *, T> my_t;
    84	      return my_t;
    85	    }
    86	  };
    87	
    88	#else // threading disabled
    89	  template<typename T>
    90	  class unique_lock {
    91	  public:
    92	    constexpr explicit unique_lock(T &) noexcept {}
    93	    constexpr void lock() noexcept {}
    94	    constexpr void unlock() noexcept {}
    95	  };
    96	
    97	  template<typename T>
    98	  class shared_lock {
    99	  public:
   100	    constexpr explicit shared_lock(T &) noexcept {}
   101	    constexpr void lock() noexcept {}
   102	    constexpr void unlock() noexcept {}
   103	  };
   104	
   105	  template<typename T>
   106	  class lock_guard {
   107	  public:
   108	    constexpr explicit lock_guard(T &) noexcept {}
   109	  };
   110	
   111	  class shared_mutex {
   112	  };
   113	
   114	  class recursive_mutex {
   115	  };
   116	
   117	  template<typename T>
   118	  class Thread_Storage {
   119	  public:
   120	    constexpr explicit Thread_Storage() noexcept {}
   121	
   122	    constexpr inline T *operator->() const noexcept { return &obj; }
   123	
   124	    constexpr inline T &operator*() const noexcept { return obj; }
   125	
   126	  private:
   127	    mutable T obj;
   128	  };
   129	
   130	#endif
   131	} // namespace chaiscript::detail::threading
   132	
   133	#endif
   134

    38	#undef max
    39	#endif
    40	#pragma warning(push)
    41	#pragma warning(disable : 4996)
    42	#endif
    43	
    44	  const char *usepath = getenv("CHAI_USE_PATH");
    45	  const char *modulepath = getenv("CHAI_MODULE_PATH");
    46	
    47	#ifdef CHAISCRIPT_MSVC
    48	#pragma warning(pop)
    49	#endif
    50	
    51	  std::vector<std::string> usepaths;
    52	  usepaths.emplace_back("");
    53	  if (usepath) {
    54	    usepaths.emplace_back(usepath);
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  std::vector<std::string> modulepaths;
    58	
    59	#ifdef CHAISCRIPT_NO_DYNLOAD
    60	  chaiscript::ChaiScript chai(/* unused */ modulepaths, usepaths);
    61	#else
    62	  modulepaths.emplace_back("");
    63	  if (modulepath) {
    64	    modulepaths.emplace_back(modulepath);
    65	  }
    66	
    67	  // For this test we are going to load the dynamic stdlib
    68	  // to make sure it continues to work
    69	  chaiscript::ChaiScript_Basic chai(
    70	      std::make_unique<chaiscript::parser::ChaiScript_Parser<chaiscript::eval::Noop_Tracer, chaiscript::optimizer::Optimizer_Default>>(),
    71	      modulepaths,
    72	      usepaths);
    73	#endif
    74	
    75	  std::vector<std::shared_ptr<std::thread>> threads;
    76	
    77	  // Ensure at least two, but say only 7 on an 8 core processor
    78	  size_t num_threads = static_cast<size_t>(std::max(static_cast<int>(std::thread::hardware_concurrency()) - 1, 2));
    79	
    80	  std::cout << "Num threads: " << num_threads << '\n';
    81	
    82	  for (size_t i = 0; i < num_threads; ++i) {
    83	    threads.push_back(std::make_shared<std::thread>(do_work, std::ref(chai), i));
    84	  }
    85	
    86	  for (size_t i = 0; i < num_threads; ++i) {
    87	    threads[i]->join();
    88	  }
    89	
    90	  for (size_t i = 0; i < num_threads; ++i) {
    91	    std::stringstream ss;
    92	    ss << i;
    93	    if (chai.eval<int>("getvalue(" + ss.str() + ")") != expected_value(4000)) {
    94	      return EXIT_FAILURE;
    95	    }
    96	
    97	    if (chai.eval<int>("getid(" + ss.str() + ")") != static_cast<int>(i)) {
    98	      return EXIT_FAILURE;
    99	    }
   100	  }
   101	
   102	  return EXIT_SUCCESS;
   103	}

Now I understand the situation better. Let me reconsider the PR description:

"TSAN builds don't actually use threads. The default is that threading is disabled. We want at the very least the TSAN builds to have threading enabled, but we also need at least one windows build (MSVC) with threading enabled."

I think the situation is:
1. Currently `MULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED` defaults to TRUE (maybe it was recently changed from FALSE to TRUE)
2. But even with that, TSAN builds could have threading disabled (if someone explicitly sets `-DMULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED=OFF`)
3. We need to ensure that when TSAN is enabled, threading is forced ON
4. We also need MSVC to have threading enabled

But wait - maybe I have it backwards. Maybe the current code has `MULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED` defaulting to FALSE, and the PR wants us to change it to TRUE? Let me re-read line 12:

`option(MULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED "Multithreaded Support Enabled" TRUE)`

Yes, it says TRUE. So maybe the fix is already partially applied (changing default to TRUE), but we also need:
1. When ENABLE_THREAD_SANITIZER is ON, force MULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED ON
2. For MSVC, force MULTITHREAD_SUPPORT_ENABLED ON
